  "content": "# client-go: Advanced Systems Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It occupies a precise position in the dependency graph: it sits **above** `apimachinery` (which owns the type system and serialization) and **below** every Kubernetes controller, operator, and CLI tool that needs to talk to the API server.\n\nIts canonical source lives in the Kubernetes monorepo under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` and is published as a standalone module at `k8s.io/client-go`. A `client-go` release `v0.X.Y` tracks Kubernetes `v1.X.Y` exactly; a client built against an older version will work against a newer server, but not the reverse (the official compatibility guarantee flows one direction only).\n\n**Upstream dependencies** (things client-go consumes):\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery` \u2014 `runtime.Object`, `schema.GroupVersionKind`, `watch.Event`, `meta.Accessor`, all error helpers (`apierrors.IsNotFound`, etc.).\n- Standard Go TLS and HTTP stacks (`net/http`, `crypto/tls`).\n- `golang.org/x/time/rate` for token-bucket rate limiting in the work queue.\n\n**Downstream dependents** (things that consume client-go):\n- Every built-in controller in `k8s.io/kubernetes` (the scheduler, the replication controller, the deployment controller, etc.).\n- Operator SDK, controller-runtime, kubebuilder, Argo, Flux \u2014 all built on the informer/work-queue pattern exposed here.\n- `kubectl` and every other CLI tool that speaks to the API server.\n\n**What client-go does NOT own:**\n- API type definitions (owned by `k8s.io/api`).\n- API server implementation (owned by `k8s.io/apiserver`).\n- Code generation tooling (owned by `k8s.io/code-generator`).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and How Responsibilities Are Split\n\n### 2.1 Configuration Layer\n\n`rest.Config` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/config.go`) is the in-memory representation of everything needed to connect to an API server. It carries transport-level concerns (TLS certificates, proxy, dial function), auth credentials (bearer token, exec-plugin config, OIDC auth provider), and policy (QPS, burst, timeout, warning handler).\n\nThere are two standard factories for `rest.Config`:\n\n- **`rest.InClusterConfig()`** (`rest/config.go:543`) reads the pod's projected service account token from `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token` and the cluster CA from the same directory, using the `KUBERNETES_SERVICE_HOST`/`KUBERNETES_SERVICE_PORT` environment variables injected by the kubelet.\n- **`tools/clientcmd`** handles the full kubeconfig file parsing, context merging, and external auth provider delegation for out-of-cluster use.\n\nThe separation is deliberate: loading a config is one concern; using it is another. The `rest.Config` struct implements `fmt.Stringer` with automatic redaction of sensitive fields (`BearerToken`, `Password`, `KeyData`) to prevent credential leakage through log output.\n\n### 2.2 REST Client Layer\n\n`rest.RESTClient` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/client.go`) is the foundational HTTP client. It provides a builder API (`Verb()`, `Resource()`, `Namespace()`, `Name()`, `SubResource()`, `Body()`) that constructs a `rest.Request` object (`rest/request.go`). Execution is deferred until a terminal method \u2014 `Do()`, `DoRaw()`, `Stream()`, or `Watch()` \u2014 is called.\n\nThe `Request` struct holds both the request construction state and the execution policy:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/request.go:96\ntype Request struct {\n    c          *RESTClient\n    rateLimiter flowcontrol.RateLimiter\n    backoff     BackoffManagerWithContext\n    timeout     time.Duration\n    maxRetries  int\n    verb        string\n    resource    string\n    resourceName string\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nThe transport layer (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/transport/transport.go`) assembles a chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects via `transport.New()`. Each link in the chain handles one concern: TLS configuration, adding the `Authorization` header (bearer token or exec-plugin token), impersonation headers, user-agent, etc. This is the mechanism for **all** authentication \u2014 it is injected at transport construction time, not at request time. Callers use `rest.Config.WrapTransport` to inject additional middleware into this chain.\n\nContent negotiation happens via the `Accept` header. Clients can request:\n- `application/json` or `application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf` for full objects.\n- `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` for metadata-only responses (a major memory optimization for large lists).\n- `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` for tabular output (used by `kubectl get`).\n\n### 2.3 Typed Clientset\n\n`kubernetes.Clientset` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/`) is a generated facade over `rest.RESTClient`. It provides a compile-time-typed, fluent interface for every built-in API group:\n\n```go\npod, err := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n```\n\nEach API group method (e.g., `CoreV1()`, `AppsV1()`) returns a group interface that exposes a `RESTClient()` method for callers who need to escape to the raw level. The clientset is constructed from a single `rest.Config` via `kubernetes.NewForConfig()`.\n\n### 2.4 Dynamic and Discovery Clients\n\n`dynamic.DynamicClient` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/dynamic/`) represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, bypassing the typed code-generation layer. This is the entry point for CRD-backed resources and is required when the resource type is not known at compile time.\n\n`discovery.DiscoveryClient` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/discovery/`) queries the API server's discovery endpoints (`/api`, `/apis`) to determine what resource types exist and what verbs they support. The `CachedDiscoveryClient` wraps it with on-disk caching (defaulting to `~/.kube/cache/discovery/`) to avoid hammering the API server on every invocation.\n\n### 2.5 Controller Infrastructure (tools/cache)\n\nThis is the most architecturally significant part of client-go. The `tools/cache` package (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/`) implements a high-throughput, low-overhead event-driven caching system that underpins every Kubernetes controller.\n\nKey types:\n\n| Type | File | Role |\n|---|---|---|\n| `Reflector` | `reflector.go` | Drives LIST+WATCH against the API server; feeds the Store |\n| `DeltaFIFO` | `delta_fifo.go` | Accumulates change events per object key, with deduplication |\n| `sharedIndexInformer` | `shared_informer.go` | Coordinates Reflector, DeltaFIFO, Indexer, and fan-out to listeners |\n| `Indexer` | `index.go` | Thread-safe local cache with secondary index support |\n| `sharedProcessor` | `shared_informer.go` | Fan-out delivery of notifications to registered handlers |\n\n### 2.6 Work Queue\n\n`util/workqueue` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/`) provides the deduplicating, rate-limited work queue that forms the boundary between the informer machinery and controller business logic.\n\n### 2.7 Leader Election\n\n`tools/leaderelection` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`) implements lease-based leader election using Kubernetes `Lease` objects or other `ResourceLock` implementations, ensuring single-writer semantics for HA controllers.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request and Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Simple Imperative Request\n\n```\nApplication code\n  \u2192 clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"ns\").Get(ctx, \"name\", opts)\n  \u2192 rest.Request.Do(ctx)           [request.go]\n  \u2192 rateLimiter.Wait(ctx)          [token bucket, flowcontrol/]\n  \u2192 http.RoundTripper chain        [transport/transport.go]\n      \u2192 auth roundtripper (injects Authorization header)\n      \u2192 TLS transport (mTLS to apiserver)\n  \u2192 API server (HTTPS)\n  \u2192 response deserialized via NegotiatedSerializer\n  \u2192 *v1.Pod returned to caller\n```\n\nIf the API server responds with HTTP 429, the `withRetry` middleware (`rest/with_retry.go`) reads the `Retry-After` header and waits before retrying (up to `maxRetries` times). Responses with non-2xx status codes are deserialized into `*apierrors.StatusError`, enabling structured checks like `apierrors.IsNotFound(err)`.\n\n### 3.2 Informer Control Loop (Event-Driven Path)\n\nThis is the critical path for all production controllers. The full data flow is:\n\n```\n[API Server]\n    |\n    | LIST (initial, paginated) then WATCH (streaming)\n    v\n[Reflector] \u2014 staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go\n    |\n    | Calls store.Replace() on initial list, then Add/Update/Delete on watch events\n    v\n[DeltaFIFO] \u2014 staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go\n    |  key \u2192 []Delta (Add, Update, Delete, Replace, Sync)\n    |\n    | controller.processLoop() pops from queue (holding DeltaFIFO lock)\n    v\n[sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas()] \u2014 shared_informer.go:716\n    |\n    | processDeltas(): for each Delta:\n    |   1. Updates the Indexer (in-memory cache + secondary indexes)\n    |   2. Calls sharedProcessor.distribute()\n    v\n[sharedProcessor] \u2014 shared_informer.go:795\n    |  Fan-out: for each registered processorListener\n    v\n[processorListener.add()] \u2014 queues notification to per-listener channel\n    |\n    | processorListener.pop() goroutine drains addCh \u2192 nextCh\n    | processorListener.run() goroutine drains nextCh, calls handler methods\n    v\n[ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd / OnUpdate / OnDelete]\n    |  (user code \u2014 informer event handler)\n    |  Should be fast; enqueue key to work queue, do NOT reconcile here\n    v\n[workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface] \u2014 util/workqueue/\n    |\n    | Worker goroutines call queue.Get(), reconcile, queue.Done()\n    | On failure: queue.AddRateLimited() with exponential backoff\n    v\n[Controller business logic]\n    |  Reads from Indexer/Lister (cache) via:\n    |  lister.Pods(\"ns\").Get(\"name\") \u2014 no API call\n    |  Writes mutations to API server via clientset\n    v\n[API Server]\n```\n\nThe `Reflector.ListAndWatchWithContext()` (`reflector.go:408`) governs the initial sync:\n1. If `WatchListClient` feature gate is enabled, it tries the more efficient streaming `watchList` path first.\n2. Otherwise (or on fallback), it calls `r.list()` which issues a paginated LIST using `tools/pager` to handle continuation tokens automatically.\n3. After the initial list, `r.watchWithResync()` starts a background goroutine for periodic resync and enters the main watch loop in `r.watch()`.\n\nThe watch loop requests bookmarks (`AllowWatchBookmarks: true`) from the API server. Bookmarks are synthetic watch events that carry an updated `resourceVersion` without representing an object change. They allow the Reflector to track progress without receiving a real event, which is critical for efficient recovery from watch restarts.\n\n**Recovery from \"too old resource version\":** When the Reflector receives an `isExpiredError`, it sets `isLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable = true` and re-lists from scratch (resource version `\"\"`), getting a fresh consistent snapshot. Watch bookmarks reduce the frequency of this expensive operation by keeping `lastSyncResourceVersion` more current.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Watch Connection Drops\n\nThe Reflector's `watch()` loop (`reflector.go:499`) is designed to be resilient. On connection drop, it catches the error, calls `watchErrorHandler`, and uses an `ExponentialBackoffManager` initialized with:\n\n```go\n// reflector.go:282\nbackoffManager: wait.NewExponentialBackoffManager(\n    800*time.Millisecond, 30*time.Second, 2*time.Minute, 2.0, 1.0, clock)\n```\n\nThis ramps from 800ms up to a 30\u201360s ceiling, reducing API server load by ~98% during outages.\n\nWatch requests carry a random timeout in `[minWatchTimeout, 2*minWatchTimeout]` (default `[5m, 10m]`) to spread reconnect load across a cluster's many informers.\n\n### 4.2 DeltaFIFO Deduplication Semantics\n\n`DeltaFIFO` accumulates per-key delta slices rather than replacing them. This means:\n- If an object is Added, Updated, and Deleted before the consumer processes it, all three deltas survive in order.\n- Double-deletes collapse: appending a `Deleted` delta when the accumulator already ends with `Deleted` is a no-op (unless the existing terminal is a `DeletedFinalStateUnknown`, which gets replaced to preserve the most accurate last state).\n\nThis is a deliberate tradeoff: no change is lost, but memory grows if the consumer is slow. The consumer (`controller.processLoop`) holds the DeltaFIFO lock for the duration of processing each key's deltas, preventing concurrent modification from the Reflector.\n\n### 4.3 Slow Handler Backpressure\n\nThe `SharedInformer` contract (`shared_informer.go:130`) is explicit: **\"A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of notifications.\"** Each `processorListener` has an internal ring buffer (`initialBufferSize = 1024`, `shared_informer.go:340`) with a separate `pop` goroutine that bridges `addCh` to `nextCh`. If the `run` goroutine (calling user code) is slow, the ring buffer grows unboundedly.\n\nThis is why the canonical pattern is for event handlers to only enqueue a key to a work queue, never to reconcile inline. The work queue provides the backpressure and retry semantics that the informer deliberately lacks.\n\n### 4.4 Late-Joining Handlers\n\nAdding an event handler to an already-running informer is safe but requires a protocol (`shared_informer.go:693`):\n1. Acquire `blockDeltas` mutex \u2014 stops all in-progress event distribution.\n2. Do a full scan of `indexer.List()` to send synthetic `Add` events for all known objects.\n3. Release mutex.\n\nThis ensures the new handler's view is consistent with the shared cache at join time, without restarting the informer.\n\n### 4.5 Client-Side Rate Limiting\n\nThe default `rest.Config` uses `QPS=5.0`, `Burst=10` (`rest/config.go:47`). These are intentionally conservative. In informer-based controllers, most reads hit the local cache (zero API calls), so the rate limit mainly governs write mutations. However, controllers that fan out to many resources (e.g., the deployment controller managing thousands of pods) can easily saturate these defaults. Operators should tune `QPS` and `Burst` based on actual write rates, and use per-resource clientsets with different configs when appropriate.\n\n### 4.6 Leader Election Tradeoffs\n\n`LeaderElector` (`leaderelection.go:116`) uses three configuration parameters:\n- `LeaseDuration` (default 15s): how long a non-leader waits before stealing a lease.\n- `RenewDeadline` (default 10s): how long the leader retries before giving up.\n- `RetryPeriod` (default 2s): polling interval.\n\nThe package comment (`leaderelection.go:28`) documents an important limitation: this implementation does **not** guarantee mutual exclusion in the presence of arbitrary clock skew or network partitions. `ReleaseOnCancel=true` creates a TOCTOU window \u2014 between the leader detecting context cancellation and the Lease being released, a new leader can be elected. This is by design for availability, not correctness. For strict fencing, an external mechanism is required.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Transport Wrapping (`rest.Config.WrapTransport`)\n\n`rest.Config.WrapTransport` (`rest/config.go:115`) is the primary hook for injecting per-request middleware into the HTTP stack. It is called after the base TLS transport is constructed and receives the existing `http.RoundTripper`. Common uses: adding custom request headers, tracing instrumentation, logging.\n\n**Risk:** Panicking or blocking in a `RoundTripper` will hang or crash all operations through that client. Middleware must propagate context cancellation correctly (`req.Context()`) and must be goroutine-safe.\n\n### 5.2 `SharedInformer.SetTransform(TransformFunc)`\n\n`TransformFunc` (`shared_informer.go:231`) is called on each object before it enters the `Indexer`. Typical use: stripping unused fields (e.g., `managedFields`, large annotation blobs) to reduce cache memory footprint.\n\n**Risk:** Must be set **before** `Run()` is called; attempting to set it after start returns an error. The transform function must be idempotent and must not retain references to the passed object (mutation is forbidden).\n\n### 5.3 `SharedInformerFactory.WithTweakListOptions`\n\n`WithTweakListOptions` (`informers/factory.go:87`) allows injecting a `TweakListOptionsFunc` that modifies every `ListOptions` before a list or watch is issued. This is the hook for field selectors and label selectors at the factory level.\n\n**Risk:** Field selectors are evaluated on the API server, not the cache. If you filter at the factory level, the Indexer only sees the filtered subset. Controller code that relies on full cluster visibility will have blind spots.\n\n### 5.4 Custom `ResourceEventHandler`\n\nRegistering handlers via `AddEventHandler` or `AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod` is the primary extension point for controllers. `ResourceEventHandlerFuncs` (`controller.go:277`) is a convenience adapter that allows implementing only a subset of `OnAdd`/`OnUpdate`/`OnDelete`.\n\n**Risk:** Handlers are called **synchronously** from the `processorListener.run()` goroutine, under no informer lock but with the constraint that they must not block. Handlers that perform synchronous API calls or hold locks that conflict with informer internals risk deadlock or cascade delays across all listeners of the same informer.\n\n### 5.5 Custom `WatchErrorHandler`\n\n`SetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext` (`shared_informer.go:220`) replaces the default error logger. Useful for feeding watch error metrics into custom monitoring systems.\n\n**Risk:** Must be set before `Run()`. The handler must return quickly \u2014 any expensive processing blocks the Reflector's reconnect cycle.\n\n### 5.6 Custom Indexers\n\n`SharedIndexInformer.AddIndexers(Indexers)` (`shared_informer.go:269`) adds secondary indexes to the Indexer. An `IndexFunc` takes an object and returns a slice of indexed values (strings). This allows efficient lookups like \"all Pods with owner reference X\" without scanning the full cache.\n\n**Risk:** Indexes must be added before `Run()`. Adding indexes to a started informer is forbidden. Index functions must be pure (no side effects) and fast; they are called on every cache mutation.\n\n### 5.7 `applyconfigurations` and Server-Side Apply\n\nThe `applyconfigurations/` package provides type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply (SSA) payloads. SSA is architecturally distinct from the traditional `get-modify-update` loop: the client declares intent declaratively, and the server merges field ownership. This allows multiple controllers to manage different fields of the same object without stomping on each other.\n\n**Risk:** SSA patches must specify a `fieldManager` identity. Callers that switch between SSA and imperative updates on the same fields can create conflict errors.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Memory Footprint of the Informer Cache\n\nEach `SharedIndexInformer` maintains a full in-memory copy of every object matching its LIST/WATCH selector. In large clusters with thousands of Pods or Events, this can amount to hundreds of MiB per controller process. The `SetTransform` hook exists specifically to address this:\n\n```go\nfactory.WithTransform(func(obj interface{}) (interface{}, error) {\n    if pod, ok := obj.(*v1.Pod); ok {\n        pod.ManagedFields = nil\n        pod.Annotations = nil // if not needed by controller logic\n    }\n    return obj, nil\n})\n```\n\nThe `sharedInformerFactory` (`informers/factory.go:57`) propagates the transform to all informers it creates via `InformerFor()`:\n\n```go\n// informers/factory.go:216\ninformer.SetTransform(f.transform)\n```\n\n### 6.2 SharedInformerFactory and Informer Deduplication\n\nThe `sharedInformerFactory` (`informers/factory.go:66`) uses `reflect.Type` as the key for its `informers` map. This means that for a given process, there is exactly one `SharedIndexInformer` per object type (per factory). Multiple controllers that watch the same type share one watch stream, one cache, and one set of event buffers \u2014 dramatically reducing API server load compared to each controller maintaining its own watch.\n\nThe `Start(stopCh)` \u2192 `WaitForCacheSync(stopCh)` sequence is the idiomatic initialization:\n\n```go\n// factory.go:144\nfunc (f *sharedInformerFactory) Start(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n    for informerType, informer := range f.informers {\n        if !f.startedInformers[informerType] {\n            f.wg.Add(1)\n            go func() {\n                defer f.wg.Done()\n                informer.Run(stopCh)\n            }()\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nCalling `Start()` after adding informers acquired post-first-start is safe; the method is idempotent per-type.\n\n### 6.3 Work Queue Backpressure and Retry Policy\n\n`DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter` (`workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go:50`) composes two limiters with `MaxOfRateLimiter`:\n- **Per-item exponential backoff**: 5ms base, 1000s ceiling (`baseDelay*2^failures`).\n- **Global token bucket**: 10 QPS, burst 100.\n\nThe effective wait for a repeatedly failing item is `max(per-item-backoff, global-bucket-wait)`. The global bucket prevents a pathological item from starving healthy items via starvation of the global limiter.\n\nWork queues also deduplicate: `Add(key)` is a no-op if `key` is already in the queue or currently being processed. This means that a flood of informer events for the same object coalesces into a single reconciliation invocation, which is the intended behavior for level-based controllers.\n\n### 6.4 Feature Gates Affecting Informer Behavior\n\n`client-go` exposes its own feature gate registry (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/features/`):\n\n- **`WatchListClient`**: When enabled (`reflector.go:300`), the Reflector prefers the streaming `WatchList` API (KEP-3157), which reduces API server memory usage for large collections by streaming objects directly rather than building a full paginated list response.\n- **`InOrderInformersBatchProcess`**: Enables batch processing of Deltas from `DeltaFIFO`, potentially improving throughput.\n- **`ClientsAllowCBOR`**: Enables CBOR serialization as an alternative to JSON/Protobuf (`rest/config.go:715`).\n\nFeature gates affect behavior at the library level; consumers must ensure their API server supports the corresponding server-side features before enabling them.\n\n### 6.5 Reflector Metrics and Observability\n\n`reflector_metrics.go` registers Prometheus-compatible metrics through a `MetricsProvider` interface (the default provider is a no-op). Operators can register a real metrics provider to expose:\n- `reflector_lists_total` / `reflector_watches_total` \u2014 watch restarts signal API server instability.\n- `reflector_last_resource_version` \u2014 used to detect a stuck reflector.\n- `reflector_watch_duration_seconds` \u2014 watch stream health.\n\nThe work queue similarly exposes queue depth, processing latency, and retry counts through `workqueue/metrics.go`.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 ARCHITECTURE.md                         # Official architecture overview\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 rest/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 config.go                           # rest.Config, InClusterConfig, RESTClientFor\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 client.go                           # RESTClient, builder pattern entry point\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 request.go                          # Request struct, Do/Watch/Stream execution\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 with_retry.go                       # WithRetry interface, withRetry impl, Retry-After handling\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 transport.go                        # HTTPClientFor, transport construction from config\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 warnings.go                         # WarningHandler, default warning logger\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 transport/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 transport.go                        # RoundTripper chain assembly, TLS config\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 kubernetes/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 clientset.go                        # kubernetes.Clientset, NewForConfig\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 dynamic/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 interface.go                        # ListerWatcher interface, ListWatch\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 listers.go                      # GenericLister, GenericNamespaceLister\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 mutation_cache.go               # MutationCache for optimistic read-your-writes\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 thread_safe_store.go            # threadSafeMap, the backing store for Indexer\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 clientcmd/                          # kubeconfig loading, context merging\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 leaderelection/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 leaderelection.go               # LeaderElector, acquire/renew loop\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 resourcelock/                   # DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter, exponential + bucket\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 flowcontrol/                        # Token bucket (RateLimiter) for REST client QPS\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 retry/                              # Retry utilities (RetryOnConflict)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 applyconfigurations/                    # Generated type-safe SSA builders\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 gentype/                                # Generic typed client helpers (post-1.28)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 features/                              # client-go-scoped feature gates (WatchListClient, etc.)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\n`client-go`'s architecture is layered and deliberately decoupled:\n\n1. **Configuration** (`rest.Config`, `clientcmd`) is separated from **execution** (`RESTClient`, `Request`).\n2. **Authentication** is injected at transport construction time via `RoundTripper` chains, not at call sites.\n3. The **informer subsystem** replaces per-reconciliation API calls with a shared, eventually-consistent local cache. The DeltaFIFO queue ensures no event is lost, while the shared processor fan-out ensures all registered handlers receive notifications sequentially and independently.\n4. The **work queue** is the architectural seam between event detection (informer) and reconciliation (controller). Its deduplication, deferred execution, and rate-limited retry semantics are what make Kubernetes controllers robust to transient failures without starvation or tight loops.\n5. **Extension** is designed around composition: `WrapTransport` for HTTP middleware, `TransformFunc` for memory optimization, `AddIndexers` for efficient cache queries, and `ResourceEventHandler` for controller logic hooks \u2014 each with clear pre-conditions (most require configuration before `Run()`) and failure modes (slow handlers, panicking middleware) that must be understood by operators.\n",

# client-go: Advanced Systems Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It occupies a precise position in the dependency graph: it sits **above** `apimachinery` (which owns the type system and serialization) and **below** every Kubernetes controller, operator, and CLI tool that needs to talk to the API server.

Its canonical source lives in the Kubernetes monorepo under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` and is published as a standalone module at `k8s.io/client-go`. A `client-go` release `v0.X.Y` tracks Kubernetes `v1.X.Y` exactly; a client built against an older version will work against a newer server, but not the reverse (the official compatibility guarantee flows one direction only).

**Upstream dependencies** (things client-go consumes):
- `k8s.io/apimachinery` — `runtime.Object`, `schema.GroupVersionKind`, `watch.Event`, `meta.Accessor`, all error helpers (`apierrors.IsNotFound`, etc.).
- Standard Go TLS and HTTP stacks (`net/http`, `crypto/tls`).
- `golang.org/x/time/rate` for token-bucket rate limiting in the work queue.

**Downstream dependents** (things that consume client-go):
- Every built-in controller in `k8s.io/kubernetes` (the scheduler, the replication controller, the deployment controller, etc.).
- Operator SDK, controller-runtime, kubebuilder, Argo, Flux — all built on the informer/work-queue pattern exposed here.
- `kubectl` and every other CLI tool that speaks to the API server.

**What client-go does NOT own:**
- API type definitions (owned by `k8s.io/api`).
- API server implementation (owned by `k8s.io/apiserver`).
- Code generation tooling (owned by `k8s.io/code-generator`).
